Oh sons, I have given you this book, which is the culmination of my knowledge in medicine, because it was my wish to die with such completion and for the explications and declarations made in it, I think that you will understand it better than anyone else by means of this treatise, which is a part of surgical art.
Because the operation in my region and in our time is done secretly, behind closed doors, although it is very perilous to the science of it, and its study is not kept; nor will I leave but a few small descriptions in the books of the Ancients, which have corrected the most and amended those errors and hesitations among them, so that their intentions may be understood, and the force of art may be extended.
And I think that you will revive that ancient order of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abridgment; and in order that it may take on the forms of the cautery instruments and of other work tools, whether by addition of the declaration or preparation of it, which is necessary.
The cause for which this art is not understood in our time, is that the art of medicine is long and that it is difficult for its actor to be exercised in the science of anatomy, which he has learned from Galen when he knew about the joints and their forms, and their connection and separation; and he knows the bones, nerves, and tendons, and their numbers and qualities; and about the pulsating veins and quiet ones, and their locations on the removal of theirs.
And so it is said that Hippocrates has this name, but in the work little and more so in the art of medicine.
But we have already said about that one in the introduction of this book; for who is not knowledgeable about it, does not understand anatomy, and therefore will not be able to escape error by which people will die, as I have seen many of those, because some of them are formed in this science and get lost from their knowledge and experiments.
That I saw a doctor mad and elderly who inflicted an abscess on the neck of a woman, and cut some arteries in the neck so that there flowed great blood within her before she died between those of hers.
And I saw another doctor who prescribed that the man swallow a piece of someone who had suffered in his condition, and the piece was large, and came to him and tore open that part further, so that that man died on the fourth day.
But I also asked to remove that one, and I saw that because of the size of the piece and due to the patient's condition it was clear to me that he would die.
I saw another doctor who received a stipend from a duke of our land for surgery, and came to a blacksmith who was causing him a fracture in his cavity; and because of the doctor's ignorance, he removed the fracture on the wound with pillows and stakes with great tightness, without laying the wound flat again.
And he took away the patient according to his desires, and took him off the pillow, and took out the lancet after some days and commanded that we should take away the bandage; and thus until the cavity and the foot were closed up, and death was approached.
And I was called to him, and I dressed his bandage, and achieved peace and cured the pain.
May corruption was already confirmed in the member, so that it could not be restrained, and the corruption did not cease to wander through the member until the illness reached its peak.
And we saw another doctor who perforated an abscess with cancer, and it became ulcerated after several days, until the cancerous power of him consumed the lord of his body.
Which cause is that the cancerous wound is pure of melancholic humors, and thus it does not penetrate to him with iron from head to toe, but rather is in a member which has suffered so that the whole was infected.

And I have already existed in this entire location of this book where there has been a victory over operation in which is error and fear; therefore it is necessary for you to guard this and lay down, so that the leaves do not get into speaking about it and deceiving you.
We take up our arms in supplication and protection of God, and our sick ones with faith and firmness.
And we use the better way through God's grace to achieve salvation and glorious succession, and let us lay away the terrible illnesses of difficult healing, and our arms from this that makes you fear, so that your sight is fixed on your faith and in our name will not evade you: for what remains is to be added to your glory, and more so in the world and in the next life than in the sanctity.

And the second is that it is dislocated from its beginning and end of the muscle, and this is done slowly; and it is not dislocated at the parts in front of the shoulder, nor at the parts behind by the joint.
And it is more severely dislocated and protrudes beyond the parts behind the joint of the tendon, and much more so in those where there are little fat, whereas in those with more fatty tissue, it is less dislocated.
Injuries often happen to acute patients with percussion or fall, and the muscle of them is inflamed from inflammation, and it's cut by this that already be dislocated.
So that you can press into this that is on while you are sitting down under it, and then process in the healing of it.
And it is known that dislocation occurs when the joint parts are left exposed due to swelling; so that you can distinguish between the muscle dislocated and the muscle sound, where you will notice differences in diversity manifesting; and you will feel at the head of the muscle a cavity with swelling due to touching the swollen part as if it were an ulcer, and the patient cannot reduce their hand to its original shape, nor be able to move that part.
